1.35em;">Warner Bros. Home Entertainment Group<br /><span style="font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros. Entertainment</a>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hbo.com">www<wbr />.hbo<wbr />.com</a></span>&#160;<span class="penicon"><a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q23633?uselang=en#P856" title="Edit this on Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this on Wikidata" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/10px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" decoding="async" width="10" height="10" style="vertical-align: text-top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/15px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Before joining Thorn EMI, HBO had an agreement deals with <a href="/wiki/Vestron_Video" title="Vestron Video">Vestron Video</a> to distribute some HBO films, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terry_Fox_Story" title="The Terry Fox Story">The Terry Fox Story</a></i>. As objections to the advent of <a href="/wiki/Home_video" title="Home video">home video</a> from factions of the entertainment industry began to die down, in November 1984, HBO partnered with independent film distributor Thorn EMI to form Thorn EMI/HBO Video.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Thorn EMI cut various distribution agreements with smaller film production companies that did not have their own home video units, such as Orion Pictures and New Line Cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-HBO_Expanding_the_Brand_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBO_Expanding_the_Brand-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 1986, <a href="/wiki/Cannon_Films" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannon Films">Cannon Films</a> bought out Thorn EMI's interest in the unit, which was accordingly renamed HBO/Cannon Video. Cannon dropped out of the venture by 1987 after the studio took a financial hit following its attempt at a series of larger budget films that did not experience box office success; the unit was then renamed HBO Video.<sup id="cite_ref-HBO_Expanding_the_Brand_41-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBO_Expanding_the_Brand-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Over time, HBO Video (which eventually became HBO Home Video in January 1994 and HBO Home Entertainment by September 5, 2009, with physical product manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Home_Video" title="Warner Home Video">Warner Home Video</a>) shifted away from releasing films from independent studios to releasing HBO's catalog of original programs and films on DVD and Blu-ray Disc.<sup id="cite_ref-HBO_Expanding_the_Brand_41-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBO_Expanding_the_Brand-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In addition, HBO Video also had some deals with other companies like Congress Video, Goodtimes Home Video, and Video Treasure to distribute HBO's catalogs and re-issued them.
</p><p>On May 8th, 2019, <a href="/wiki/WarnerMedia" title="WarnerMedia">WarnerMedia</a> (the parent company of HBO) announced that its Home Entertainment division will soon be transfer and move to <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Home_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Home Entertainment">Warner Bros. Home Entertainment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandising">Merchandising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HBO&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Merchandising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Various products have been marketed that have used the HBO trademark and/or are based around the channel's programming. In 2005, HBO entered into an agreement with <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mobility" title="AT&amp;T Mobility">Cingular Wireless</a> to establish HBO Mobile, a pre-<a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> era mobile web service.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Operating as a pay service (a model similar to that used by the channel itself), HBO Mobile featured information on HBO's original programming (including episode guides), <a href="/wiki/Mobile_wallpaper" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile wallpaper">mobile wallpapers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ringtone" title="Ringtone">ringtones</a> voiced by cast members of the channel's series (HBO Mobile also operated a similar service, HBO Family Mobile, which offered full-length episodes of the channel's children's programming). That same year, <a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Screenlife" class="mw-redirect" title="Screenlife">Screenlife</a> released a version of the DVD interactive game <i><a href="/wiki/Scene_It%3F" title="Scene It?">Scene It?</a></i>, featuring trivia relating to HBO's original series.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding">Branding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HBO&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Branding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When HBO launched in 1972, its original logo merely consisted of the "Home Box Office" name and a ticket stub surrounded by a lighted <a href="/wiki/Marquee_(sign)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marquee (sign)">marquee</a>. The original version of its current logo (designed by Bemis Balkind) was introduced in 1975, using an uppercase bold "HBO" text with a circle inside the 'O', which in turn cuts into the 'B'. The logo was modified in 1980 (although it did not completely replace the original version until 1981), with the 'B' and the 'O' becoming full letterforms, albeit continuing to be attached to each other. The simplicity of the logo makes it fairly easy to duplicate, something HBO has taken advantage of many times over the years.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HBO_New_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/HBO_New_Logo.png/140px-HBO_New_Logo.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/HBO_New_Logo.png/210px-HBO_New_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/HBO_New_Logo.png/280px-HBO_New_Logo.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="270" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HBO_New_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Glossed variant of current HBO logo, used since July 5, 2014.</div></div></div>
<p>The logo became iconic due to a program opening sequence produced in 1981 by New York City production firm <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Studios" title="Liberty Studios">Liberty Studios</a>, nicknamed "HBO in Space", which was used from September 20, 1982 to September 30, 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The original full version begins with a window shot of a family (or alternately, a married couple) in an apartment sitting down to watch HBO on their television set (which was replaced by a cloudscape that faded into the city sequence in December 1983), which transitions to a fly-through over a constructed model cityscape and countryside. A starburst—or "stargate effect"—then occurs following a pan towards a star-filled sky (which begins a shorter version of the sequence), unveiling a chrome-plated HBO logo that flies and rotates into view; colored light beams encircle the side of the "O", then flash to a partially animated sequence featuring more lights racing counter-clockwise in its interior on a silver axis, revealing "HBO Feature Presentation" or another program type (such as "<a href="/wiki/Standing_Room_Only_(TV_series)" title="Standing Room Only (TV series)">Standing Room Only</a>", "HBO Special", "On Location" and "HBO Family Showcase") in block text, before additional beams sweep across the text and shine, with more flashing into a fade to black. Most variants of this sequence were discontinued in 1986, except for the feature presentation (which was relegated to use only for the main prime time film), "<a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_at_the_Movies_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Saturday Night at the Movies (disambiguation)">Saturday Night Movie</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint Inline-Template" style="vertical-align:text-top;white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dispenser.info.tm/~dispenser/cgi-bin/dab_solver.py?page=HBO&amp;editintro=Template:Disambiguation_needed/editintro&amp;client=Template:Dn"><span title="Link needs disambiguation. (October 2019)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>" and "Sunday Night Movie" variants (the latter two of which were discontinued in 1993). Many versions of the intro are available on YouTube, including one uploaded to HBO's official YouTube channel.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The accompanying fanfare—originally composed for <a href="/wiki/Score_Productions" title="Score Productions">Score Productions</a> by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Jay_Smith_III" title="Ferdinand Jay Smith III">Ferdinand Jay Smith III</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jay_Advertising" title="Jay Advertising">Jay Advertising</a>, who adapted the theme from the Scherzo movement of <a href="/wiki/Anton%C3%ADn_Dvo%C5%99%C3%A1k" title="Antonín Dvořák">Antonín Dvořák</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Dvo%C5%99%C3%A1k)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Dvořák)">Ninth Symphony</a>—has become a musical signature for HBO, and has been used in feature presentation, upcoming program and evening schedule bumpers, and network IDs since 1998 with various arrangements from <a href="/wiki/French_horn" title="French horn">horns</a> to piano being used over the years.
</p><p>Another well-known HBO program opener produced by <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Data_Images" title="Pacific Data Images">Pacific Data Images</a>, "Neon Lights", began movies airing outside of primetime from November 1, 1986, to September 30, 1997. The sequence, set to a synth and electric guitar theme, begins with a <a href="/wiki/Heliotrope_(color)" title="Heliotrope (color)">heliotrope</a> HBO logo on a film strip with blue, green and pink light rays shooting through it as the strip rotates out of view; the lights shoot through several glowing CG slots until a flash of light hits a field of spheres in varying colors, which zoom out to form a light purple HBO logo overlaid by a cursive magenta "Movie" script against a black background with rows of light purple spheres.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> From 1997 to 1999, HBO used several feature presentation bumpers designed by Pittard Sullivan featuring the network logo in different situations (such as a fish in water, a celebrity in a <a href="/wiki/Limousine" title="Limousine">limousine</a>, a large HBO logo chasing a man and a neon HBO logo on the rooftop of a building); these sequences were also used by the network as IDs from 1997 to 2002, and in upcoming program and evening schedule bumpers until 2000.
</p><p>From September 1999 to April 1, 2011, HBO used a Pittard Sullivan-designed <a href="/wiki/CGI_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="CGI Group">CGI</a> feature presentation bumper sequence that features a flyover similar to the 1982 sequence, starting with the front of a movie theater featuring a marquee that reads "HBO Feature Presentation", and trekking through a country road, a snowy mountain road near a cliff and a desert road (respectively passing under a tower, tunnel and tanker truck shaped in the individual letters of the HBO logotype); this leads into a road in an urban neighborhood (with skyscrapers visible in the background) that becomes a bridge upon the city's downtown area, and lead to a slowing flyover toward and pan over an HBO logo-shaped lake that starts with several spotlights rapidly turning on and ends with a 3D animation of the "Feature Presentation" text. The closing animation that is seen both in the full version as well as a shorter version of the sequence (seen outside of weekend prime time films and Saturday film premieres, when the longer sequence was used).<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The sequence was replaced on April 2, 2011—as part of a new graphics package implemented on that date across the HBO multiplex channels—by a much shorter opening sequence designed by Jesse Vartanian (who also designed CGI teaser commercials for HBO's premiere telecast of the 2010 film <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i>), consisting only of a dark background with faint light auroras around the HBO logo and a simple "Feature Presentation" text animation, accompanied by soft orchestral music.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another new opening sequence, done by Imaginary Forces, was implemented on March 4, 2017. The current intro combines live-action and CGI while also paying homage to the original 1982 sequence (to the point that the latter can be seen during the new intro).<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike other pay television networks (including the multiplex channels of sister channel Cinemax), HBO does not brand its programming with <a href="/wiki/Digital_on-screen_graphic" title="Digital on-screen graphic">on-screen logo bugs</a> of the main network and each respective multiplex channel—although its multiplex channels do display logo bugs during promotional breaks between programs.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Network_slogans">Network slogans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HBO&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Network slogans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Source:</i><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_versions">International versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HBO&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: International versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HBO_(international)" title="HBO (international)">HBO (international)</a></div>
<p>Since 1991, HBO has overseen a number of partnerships that operate HBO-branded television networks around the world. As the network was launched in new markets, the HBO brand has been used in several countries. HBO has established channels in various countries worldwide including <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, Canada, <a href="/wiki/HBO_Europe" title="HBO Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="The Caribbean">the Caribbean</a>, and Southeast Asia.
</p><p>HBO also licenses its programming to air on certain other broadcast, cable channels and <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">video on demand</a> services outside the United States, such as:
</p>
<ul><li>Amedia Home of HBO, which is available in Russia.</li>
<li>OSN Home of HBO, which is available throughout the MENA region.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sky_Atlantic" title="Sky Atlantic">Sky Atlantic</a>, which is available within the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, the United Kingdom, Italy, Germany, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ziggo" title="Ziggo">Ziggo Movies &amp; Series XL</a>, Video on demand service in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HBO_Nordic" class="mw-redirect" title="HBO Nordic">HBO Nordic</a>, Video on demand service in <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>.</li>
<li>HBO Baltics, Video on demand service in <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/M-Net" title="M-Net">M-net EDGE</a> which is available in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Sahara_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Sahara Africa">Sub-Sahara Africa</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hotstar" title="Hotstar">Hotstar</a> which is an on demand service owned by <a href="/wiki/Star_India" title="Star India">Star India</a>, streams the HBO Originals content in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TVCine" title="TVCine">TVCine</a>, which is a TV cable network in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.</li>
<li>HBO Portugal, Video on demand service in Portugal.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Melita_(telecommunications_company)" title="Melita (telecommunications company)">Melita More</a>, a cable television network available in Malta and Gozo.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Be_1" title="Be 1">Be 1</a>, a Belgian French-language TV cable channel which also provides on demand service.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Showcase_(Australian_TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Showcase (Australian TV channel)">FOX Showcase</a>, an Australian cable TV channel provided on <a href="/wiki/Foxtel" title="Foxtel">Foxtel</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SoHo_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="SoHo (TV channel)">SoHo</a>, which is a TV satellite network in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.</li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Captain_Midnight_broadcast_signal_intrusion" title="Captain Midnight broadcast signal intrusion">Captain Midnight (HBO)</a>, a 1986 incident in which HBO's signal was jammed to protest the scrambling of its signal for satellite dish users</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/HBO_Films" title="HBO Films">HBO Films</a></li>
